         <h1 class="article_title" itemprop="headline name">
          The 50 Most Iconic Pictures in Sports History
         </h1>
         <h4 class="article_author" itemprop="author">
          <address class="article_author-info" itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
           By
           <a class="article_author-link" href="/users/456335-zack-pumerantz" itemprop="url" title="Zack Pumerantz">
            <span itemprop="name">
             Zack  Pumerantz
            </span>
           </a>
           ,
           <span class="author-rank">
            Analyst
           </span>
          </address>
          <time class="article_timestamp" data-updated_at="1347342445" itemprop="datePublished">
           Sep 11, 2012
          </time>
         </h4>

          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            Fourth period History was a class rarely enjoyed by drooling teenagers too busy scribbling their crush's names into desks to embrace a high school education. But when it comes to sports, these same dudes are furiously jotting down the past into their notebooks so they never forget a moment.
           </p>
           <p>
            As we prepare to trace the past and present of elite athletics, the art of sports photography must be the main focus. A picture truly is worth a thousand words.
           </p>
           <p>
            Get ready to embrace a visual feast with the 50 most iconic pictures in sports history.
           </p>
           <p>
            Capturing history, one snapshot at a time.
           </p>
          </div>

          </a>
         </section>

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             50. Ozzie Smith's Patented Flip
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="50. Ozzie Smith's Patented Flip" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/584/314/tumblr_lsyodcGTod1qm9rypo1_1280_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="630">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">
             <span itemprop="caption">
              Image via siphotos.tumblr.com
             </span>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            Simply known as The Wizard...of Oz, shortstop Ozzie Smith was more of a lion tamer when it came to calming a frantic line drive. No roaring hit was too sharp for the infield magician.
           </p>
           <p>
            And while he won 13 consecutive
            <span class="mw-redirect">
             Gold Glove Award
            </span>
            s, the speedster could also swing that pine. A .262 average, 2,460 hits and 580 steals aren't too shabby.
           </p>
           <p>
            Smith's acrobatic ability was always on display during his traditional pregame back flips.
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>
         <section class="article_page article_page--secondary js-article-page-3 cf display-none " data-page="3">
          <header class="article_page-header">
           <div class="article_nav-bar br-texture--sudo br-texture--sudo-fade-to-white">
            <div class="paginators paginators--top">

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             49. Joe Namath's Flair
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:519px">
            <img alt="49. Joe Namath's Flair" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/583/958/Bc-jtcgCGkKGrHqEH-CkEquVK52JBK22rbuI_3_crop_north.jpg?w=519&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="519"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="519">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="519">
             <span itemprop="caption">
              Image via ebay.com
             </span>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            While the image of Namath
            <a href="http://www.findingdulcinea.com/docroot/dulcinea/fd_images/news/on-this-day/On-this-Day--The-New-York-Jets-beat-the-Baltimore-Colts-in-Super-Bowl-III/news/0/image.jpg" target="_blank">
             coming through on his Super Bowl guarantee
            </a>
            over Don Shula's Colts in 1969 remains a close second, it was Broadway Joe's furred style that cemented his legacy.
           </p>
           <p>
            Seemingly the first to rep the fur coat and a pair of Ray-Bans on the bench, Namath became a New York icon. Revered for his fashion and arm, despised for his pretentious approach.
           </p>
           <p>
            A man on an island.
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>
         <section class="article_page article_page--secondary js-article-page-4 cf display-none " data-page="4">
          <header class="article_page-header">
           <div class="article_nav-bar br-texture--sudo br-texture--sudo-fade-to-white">
            <div class="paginators paginators--top">
             <a class="paginator paginator--secondary paginator--prev" href="javascript: void(0)" title="Previous Page">

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             48. Oscar Pistorius Defies the Odds
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="48. Oscar Pistorius Defies the Odds" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/583/006/oscar-pistorius-2012-olympics_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="630">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">
             <span itemprop="caption">
              Image via thefw.com
             </span>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            Dubbed the Blade Runner by inspired pundits, 25-year-old South African runner Oscar Pistorius is continuously admired for his athletic heroism and
            <a href="http://bleacherreport.com/articles/1195225-blade-runner-oscar-pistorius-a-symbol-of-spirit-worldwide" target="_blank">
             inspirational story
            </a>
            .
           </p>
           <p>
            Because he was born without fibulas, Pistorius had his legs amputated before his first birthday. But that didn't stop the determined competitor, as he recently became the first bilateral (double-limb)amputee to compete in sprinting.
           </p>
           <p>
            Following stressful
            <a href="http://thefw.com/oscar-pistorius-2012-olympics/" target="_blank">
             legal battles with the International Association of Athletics Federation
            </a>
            , Pistorius worked his way onto the able-bodied track. He's now carving his name into the history books.
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>
         <section class="article_page article_page--secondary js-article-page-5 cf display-none " data-page="5">
          <header class="article_page-header">
           <div class="article_nav-bar br-texture--sudo br-texture--sudo-fade-to-white">
            <div class="paginators paginators--top">

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             47. Magic Johnson's Hook
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:293px">
            <img alt="47. Magic Johnson's Hook" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/583/002/6a00d8341c630a53ef014e610949c2970c-800wi_crop_north.jpg?w=293&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="293"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="293">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="293">
             <span itemprop="caption">
              Image via lakersblog.latimes.com
             </span>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            Magic Johnson was revered for his versatility and fast-paced dominance. It was his junior skyhook over heated rival Larry Bird in Game 4 of the '87 Finals that cemented his legend.
           </p>
           <p>
            This baby teardrop propelled the Lakers to a 107-106 victory and the title in six games, and earned the man nicknamed "Showtime" a Finals MVP Award.
           </p>
           <p>
            A darling image of Magic's
            <a href="http://latimesblogs.latimes.com/sports_blog/2011/04/lakers-moments-magic-johnson-and-the-infamous-baby-skyhook.html" target="_blank">
             final war with the Celtics
            </a>
            .
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>
         <section class="article_page article_page--secondary js-article-page-6 cf display-none " data-page="6">
          <header class="article_page-header">
           <div class="article_nav-bar br-texture--sudo br-texture--sudo-fade-to-white">
            <div class="paginators paginators--top">

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             46. Satchel Paige's Kick
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:321px">
            <img alt="46. Satchel Paige's Kick" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/583/007/232323232ngo8486rdeduvgwuh98hi5d565d6gd2e-6238e89c7cedot1lsi_crop_north.jpg?w=321&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="321"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="321">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="321">
             <span itemprop="caption">
              Image via snapfish.com
             </span>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            The first player to be inducted into the Hall of Fame from the Negro leagues, Leroy "Satchel" Paige was an ironman long before the term ironman was popularized.
           </p>
           <p>
            After completely annihilating the Negro Leagues for over 20 years, Paige jumped on the integration train and joined the Major Leagues. At the tender age of 42, Paige became the oldest rookie ever.
           </p>
           <p>
            His windmill windup and sky-high kick made him a spectacle on major league diamonds. He was beloved for his old-school brilliance.
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>
         <section class="article_page article_page--secondary js-article-page-7 cf display-none " data-page="7">
          <header class="article_page-header">
           <div class="article_nav-bar br-texture--sudo br-texture--sudo-fade-to-white">
            <div class="paginators paginators--top">
             <a class="paginator paginator--secondary paginator--prev" href="javascript: void(0)" title="Previous Page">

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             45. The Wayne Gretzky Trade
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:620px">
            <img alt="45. The Wayne Gretzky Trade" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/583/697/30for30espngretzkytrade_crop_north.jpg?w=620&amp;h=400&amp;q=75" height="400" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="620"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="620">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="620">
             <span itemprop="caption">
              Image via dvddisk.net
             </span>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            When hockey's greatest legend was traded to the Kings two hours after his Oilers won the Stanley Cup in 1988, fans were heartbroken and shocked. Whispers of "traitor" and "he deserted us" flooded sports talk shows in Canada.
           </p>
           <p>
            But after his first game back in Edmonton, Gretzky had some calming
            <a href="http://www.tampabay.com/sports/football/bucs/how-famous-athletes-fared-returning-to-the-city-where-they-made-their-fame/1048591" target="_blank">
             words for his doubters
            </a>
            :
           </p>
           <blockquote>
            <p>
             I'm still proud to be a Canadian. I didn't desert my country. I moved  because I was traded, and that's where my job is. But I'm Canadian to  the core. I hope Canadians understand that.
            </p>
           </blockquote>
          </div>
         </section>

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             44. Ernie Davis Breaks Barriers
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:320px">
            <img alt="44. Ernie Davis Breaks Barriers" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/583/586/ernie-davis_display_image_crop_north.jpg?w=320&amp;h=400&amp;q=75" height="400" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="320"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="320">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="320">
             <span itemprop="caption">
              Image via theelmiraexpress.blogspot.com
             </span>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            As fast as Ernie Davis became a national icon, he was gone.
           </p>
           <p>
            Davis led the Syracuse Orangemen to their only national football championship in 1959 (an undefeated season) and became the first
            <span class="mw-redirect">
             African-American
            </span>
            athlete to win the Heisman Trophy as a senior in 1961. But soon after being chosen with the first pick of the '62 draft by the Redskins and then being traded to the Browns, Davis was diagnosed with leukemia.
           </p>
           <p>
            He died at the young age of 23, his legacy firmly intact.
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>
         <section class="article_page article_page--secondary js-article-page-9 cf display-none " data-page="9">
          <header class="article_page-header">
           <div class="article_nav-bar br-texture--sudo br-texture--sudo-fade-to-white">
            <div class="paginators paginators--top">
             <a class="paginator paginator--secondary paginator--prev" href="javascript: void(0)" title="Previous Page">

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             43. Curt Schilling's Bloody Sock
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:355px">
            <img alt="43. Curt Schilling's Bloody Sock" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/583/275/BloodySock_crop_north.jpg?w=355&amp;h=355&amp;q=75" height="355" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="355"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="355">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="355">
             <span itemprop="caption">
              Image via minorleagueuniversity.blogspot.com
             </span>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            With a career postseason record of 112, Curt Schilling was clearly a gamer when the moment called for a clutch performance.
           </p>
           <p>
            It was known that Schilling pitched Game 6 of the miraculous 2004 ALCS against the favored Yankees on an injured ankle, but few realized how serious it was. His bloodied sock made believers out of a beleaguered fanbase, as the Sawx would eventually become the first team in MLB history to come back from a  three-games-to-none deficit.
           </p>
           <p>
            The curse would soon be broken, thanks to Schilling's sacrifice.
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>
         <section class="article_page article_page--secondary js-article-page-10 cf display-none " data-page="10">
          <header class="article_page-header">
           <div class="article_nav-bar br-texture--sudo br-texture--sudo-fade-to-white">

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             42. Bjorn Borg Kneels in Victory
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:308px">
            <img alt="42. Bjorn Borg Kneels in Victory" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/583/323/bjorn-borg_crop_north.jpg?w=308&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="308"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="308">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="308">
             <span itemprop="caption">
              Image via worldtennismagazine.com
             </span>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            While winning five consecutive
            <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Championships,_Wimbledon" title="The Championships, Wimbledon">
             Wimbledon
            </a>
            singles titles (a record since matched by
            <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roger_Federer" title="Roger Federer">
             Roger Federer
            </a>
            ), Bjorn Borg was revered for his emotionless demeanor and grace under pressure.
           </p>
           <p>
            It was his rivalry with fiery, tantrum-filled John McEnroe that truly cemented his legend. And this was the magical moment when the calm Swede achieved that fifth Wimbledon victory, over McEnroe of course, shaping tennis forever.
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>
         <section class="article_page article_page--secondary js-article-page-11 cf display-none " data-page="11">
          <header class="article_page-header">
           <div class="article_nav-bar br-texture--sudo br-texture--sudo-fade-to-white">
            <div class="paginators paginators--top">
             <a class="paginator paginator--secondary paginator--prev" href="javascript: void(0)" title="Previous Page">
              <span class="aquo">

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             41. Jacques Plante Trademarks the Mask
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:417px">
            <img alt="41. Jacques Plante Trademarks the Mask" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/584/277/Top-10-MOMENT-Plantes-Broken-Nose-The-Hockey-Mask_crop_north.jpg?w=417&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="417"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="417">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="417">
             <span itemprop="caption">
              Image via infinit8monkeys.com
             </span>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            The only man to eventually fashion the fiberglass mask better than Jason Voorhees in
            <em>
             Friday the 13th
            </em>
            , goaltending legend Jacques Plante was as tough as they come.
           </p>
           <p>
            But on November 1, 1959, everything changed. The Rangers' Andy Bathgate nailed Plante with a shot that broke his nose. Not unexpected in those days, considering masks weren't applied. Rather than a resulting media hoopla and a fury of ambulances, Plante was taken to the locker room for stitches and a protective mask (routine in those days).
           </p>
           <p>
            The rejuvenated Canadiens then went
            <a href="http://infinit8monkeys.com/all-time-top-10-moment-jacques-plantes-hockey-mask/" target="_blank">
             18 straight games
            </a>
            without a loss behind their newly-fashioned goalie, and protective masks were cemented for good.
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>
         <section class="article_page article_page--secondary js-article-page-12 cf display-none " data-page="12">
          <header class="article_page-header">
           <div class="article_nav-bar br-texture--sudo br-texture--sudo-fade-to-white">
            <div class="paginators paginators--top">

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             40. Jim Valvano's Miraculous Upset
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="40. Jim Valvano's Miraculous Upset" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/583/810/houston1983_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="630">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">
             <span itemprop="caption">
              Image via sk1wbw.com
             </span>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            With Clyde Drexler and Hakeem Olajuwon leading the way, the 31-2, dunk-heavy Houston Cougars were essentially invincibleuntil Jim Valvano's Cinderella Wolfpack arrived.
           </p>
           <p>
            When the game ended 54-52, Valvano ran up and down "The Pit" (the Albuquerque arena) in utter bewilderment. His six-seeded Wolfpack had just upset the first-seeded team. A breathtaking March Madness moment.
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>
         <section class="article_page article_page--secondary js-article-page-13 cf display-none " data-page="13">

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             39. Eddie Gaedel Breaks the Mold
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="39. Eddie Gaedel Breaks the Mold" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/583/553/Eddie-Gaedel_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="630">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">
             <span itemprop="caption">
              Image via worthpoint.com
             </span>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            According to
            <a href="http://www.press.uchicago.edu/Misc/Chicago/852180.html" target="_blank">
             then-owner Bill Veeck
            </a>
            , "He was, by golly, the best darn midget who ever played big-league ball. He was also the only one."
           </p>
           <p>
            Eddie Gaedel made the St. Louis Browns an integral part of history when he walked up to the plate in the second game of a St. Louis Browns' doubleheader on Aug. 19, 1951, standing 3'7" and weighing only 65 pounds. After watching four straight balls fly by and a pinch runner take his spot on first, Gaedel's intriguing career was over.
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             38. Battle of the Sexes
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:275px">
            <img alt="38. Battle of the Sexes" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/583/003/09.20_crop_north.jpg?w=275&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="275"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="275">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="275">
             <span itemprop="caption">
              Image via nytimes.com
             </span>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            During her brilliant career, Billie Jean King won 12 Grand Slam singles titles, 16 Grand Slam women's doubles titles and 11 Grand Slam mixed doubles titles while pioneering the way for sexual equality.
           </p>
           <p>
            But when she athletically disrobed "
            <a href="http://www.nytimes.com/2005/08/21/books/review/21JENNING.html" target="_blank">
             male chauvinistic pig
            </a>
            " Bobby Riggs in front of the world during the 1973 Battle of the Sexes, she secured a victory for all female tennis playersrather, all female athletes.
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             37. The American Dream
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:414px">
            <img alt="37. The American Dream" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/583/430/628x471_crop_north.jpg?w=414&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="414"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="414">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="414">
             <span itemprop="caption">
              Image via sfgate.com
             </span>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            Brandi Chastain's game-winning penalty
            <span class="mw-redirect">
             shootout goal
            </span>
            against
            <span class="mw-redirect">
             China
            </span>
            in the 1999 FIFA Women's World Cup final put her in the record books for good. Her bra-filled celebration made her a legend.
           </p>
           <p>
            A euphoric moment for American soccer fans, frozen in time forever.
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>
         <section class="article_page article_page--secondary js-article-page-16 cf display-none " data-page="16">
          <header class="article_page-header">
           <div class="article_nav-bar br-texture--sudo br-texture--sudo-fade-to-white">

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             36. Vladimir Konstantinov Hoists the Cup
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:291px">
            <img alt="36. Vladimir Konstantinov Hoists the Cup" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/584/180/w2ofp_crop_north.jpg?w=291&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="291"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="291">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="291">
             <span itemprop="caption">
              Image via thehockeyguys.net
             </span>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            Six days after his Red Wings won the '97 Stanley Cup, defenseman Vladimir Konstantinov was the passenger in a tragic limousine accident. He spent several weeks in a coma and was left
            <a href="http://sports.espn.go.com/nhl/playoffs/2009/news?columnist=garber_greg&amp;id=4133702" target="_blank">
             permanently paralyzed from the waste down
            </a>
            .
           </p>
           <p>
            When the Wings successfully defended their title and brought home the '98 Cup, they brought Konstantinov onto the ice to celebrate. Despite the doctors saying he'd never play again, his locker remained intact and his teammates sported patches honoring him all season long.
           </p>
           <p>
            This was the powerful visual.
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>
         <section class="article_page article_page--secondary js-article-page-17 cf display-none " data-page="17">
          <header class="article_page-header">
           <div class="article_nav-bar br-texture--sudo br-texture--sudo-fade-to-white">

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             35. An Infused Rivalry
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:600px">
            <img alt="35. An Infused Rivalry" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/583/861/Julius-Erving-Larry-Bird_crop_north.jpg?w=600&amp;h=411&amp;q=75" height="411" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="600"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="600">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="600">
             <span itemprop="caption">
              Image via pixmule.com
             </span>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            When the Sixers acquired Julius Erving before the 1977 season and the Celtics drafted Larry Bird in 1978, an already fierce rivalry was breathed new life.
           </p>
           <p>
            Wilt Chamberlain vs. Bill Russell, Erving vs. Bird, who's next...Andrew Bynum vs. Fab Melo?
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             34. One Yard Short
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:590px">
            <img alt="34. One Yard Short" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/583/001/Dyson_crop_north.jpg?w=590&amp;h=414&amp;q=75" height="414" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="590"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="590">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="590">
             <span itemprop="caption">
              Image via blogs.thescore.com
             </span>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            Dubbed "The Tackle," Kevin Dyson's last-second stretch to unbelievably lose Super Bowl XXXIV by one yard to the Rams remains a fixture on the football field.
           </p>
           <p>
            Six seconds left, Titans losing 23-16, hearts around the gridiron world racing faster than Richard Lee Petty in the '76 Daytona 500. Most expected Steve "Air" McNair to scramble for a 10-yard score, but instead he tossed it over the middle to an open Dyson in what would become arguably the most heartbreaking moment in Titans history.
           </p>
           <p>
            Mike Jones with the tackle. A single yard.
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>
         <section class="article_page article_page--secondary js-article-page-19 cf display-none " data-page="19">
          <header class="article_page-header">
           <div class="article_nav-bar br-texture--sudo br-texture--sudo-fade-to-white">
            <div class="paginators paginators--top">

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             33. The Babe Bows Out
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="33. The Babe Bows Out" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/583/010/babe-ruth-bows-out2-jpg_crop_north.jpeg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="630">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">
             <span itemprop="caption">
              Image via iconicphotos.wordpress.com
             </span>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            It's been said that less is more. On this overcast day in 1948, Pulitzer Prize-winning photographer Nat Fein followed suit and let subtlety detail impact.
            <em>
            </em>
           </p>
           <p>
            The man who essentially "built" Yankee Stadium and sparked the live-ball era, Babe Ruth was on an island during this '48 shot. Hunched over, separate from the others, using his bat as a cane, Ruth honorably bowed out due to health issues.
           </p>
           <p>
            He would die two months later from pneumonia.
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>
         <section class="article_page article_page--secondary js-article-page-20 cf display-none " data-page="20">
          <header class="article_page-header">
           <div class="article_nav-bar br-texture--sudo br-texture--sudo-fade-to-white">
            <div class="paginators paginators--top">
             <a class="paginator paginator--secondary paginator--prev" href="javascript: void(0)" title="Previous Page">

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             32. Jason McElwain Inspires the World
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:414px">
            <img alt="32. Jason McElwain Inspires the World" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/583/914/JasonMc_crop_north.jpg?w=414&amp;h=275&amp;q=75" height="275" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="414"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="414">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="414">
             <span itemprop="caption">
              Image via brendaabee.blogspot.com
             </span>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            Diagnosed with autism at a young age, Jason McElwain was driven by his passion for basketball. Greece Athena High School basketball coach Jim Johnson even appointed him manager of the team.
           </p>
           <p>
            With a large lead in the final game and four minutes remaining, Johnson decided to put McElwain in. After two missed shots, McElwain drained six
            <span class="mw-redirect">
             three-pointers
            </span>
            and one two-point shot. A legendary 20 points in four minutes to be precise.
           </p>
           <p>
            As the buzzer went off, an inspired crowd rushed the court and carried their new icon toward immortality.
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>
         <section class="article_page article_page--secondary js-article-page-21 cf display-none " data-page="21">
          <header class="article_page-header">
           <div class="article_nav-bar br-texture--sudo br-texture--sudo-fade-to-white">
            <div class="paginators paginators--top">

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             31. The 1982 Big Game
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:556px">
            <img alt="31. The 1982 Big Game" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/584/134/morgue17-the-play_crop_north.jpg?w=556&amp;h=400&amp;q=75" height="400" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="556"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="556">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="556">
             <span itemprop="caption">
              Image via democraticunderground.com
             </span>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            The annual Big Game between Stanford and Cal reached its pinnacle in 1982, when a 20-19 lead with seconds remaining was miraculously tarnished.
           </p>
           <p>
            "The band is out on the field!"
           </p>
           <p>
            In what would become the most exciting, mysterious and quirky play in  college football history, the Cal Golden Bears took the
            <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=0fZCCAqoSwY" target="_blank">
             last-second  kickoff return to the house
            </a>
            , using a handful of laterals and a misguided band to  break Stanford's heart, 25-20.
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>
         <section class="article_page article_page--secondary js-article-page-22 cf display-none " data-page="22">
          <header class="article_page-header">
           <div class="article_nav-bar br-texture--sudo br-texture--sudo-fade-to-white">
            <div class="paginators paginators--top">

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             30. Diego Maradona Takes on Belgium
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="30. Diego Maradona Takes on Belgium" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/583/551/2_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>

            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">

             </span>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            As this Argentinian legend prepared to rumble through this gauntlet of Belgium defenders, it became clear Diego Maradona was no match for mere mortals.
           </p>
           <p>
            Despite the splitting of the opposing wall, all eyes remained focused on one man.
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>
         <section class="article_page article_page--secondary js-article-page-23 cf display-none " data-page="23">
          <header class="article_page-header">
           <div class="article_nav-bar br-texture--sudo br-texture--sudo-fade-to-white">

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             29. Secretariat Crushes the Competition
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:524px">
            <img alt="29. Secretariat Crushes the Competition" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/584/247/SecretariatThePhoto_crop_north.jpg?w=524&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="524"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="524">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="524">
             <span itemprop="caption">
              Image via thesportsmith.blogspot.com
             </span>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            Mentioned alongside the greatest thoroughbreds of all time, Secretariat was a large chestnut colt who absolutely demolished his competition back in 1973.
           </p>
           <p>
            While becoming the first Triple Crown champion in 25 years, Big Red set race records in all three races that remain today.
           </p>
           <p>
            An empty look back gave jockey Ron Turcotte the realization that few could compete with his horse.
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>
         <section class="article_page article_page--secondary js-article-page-24 cf display-none " data-page="24">
          <header class="article_page-header">
           <div class="article_nav-bar br-texture--sudo br-texture--sudo-fade-to-white">

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             28. Bill Buckner's Botch
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="28. Bill Buckner's Botch" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/583/273/bill-buckner-1_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="630">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">
             <span itemprop="caption">
              Image via thegloryofbaseball.blogspot.com
             </span>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            With the Sawx a mere out away from their first championship since  1918, the scrutinized curse seemed to be nearing an end. That was until the Mets hit three straight singles to cut their deficit to 5-4.
           </p>
           <p>
            Veteran Bob  Stanley was called on in relief and quickly added salt to the wound, tossing one to the backstop that tied the game (although we believe it was a passed ball on catcher Rich Gedman). Next came Mookie Wilson, who  hit a slow dribbler to first base.
           </p>
           <p>
            Bill Buckner's five-hole fiasco remains a fixture, as it gave New York the victory and forced a Game 7. Which, as we all know, led to Boston's drought remaining firmly intact.
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>
         <section class="article_page article_page--secondary js-article-page-25 cf display-none " data-page="25">

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             27. Pele Hovers Above
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:243px">
            <img alt="27. Pele Hovers Above" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/584/092/pele_crop_north.jpg?w=243&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="243"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="243">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="243">
             <span itemprop="caption">
              Image via sites.duke.edu
             </span>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            Few athletes have demanded such respect, few have engaged such worship, and few have dominated so eloquently.
           </p>
           <p>
            This shot captured the godly effect that Pele had on peers, fans and pundits as he towered over his mortal audience. The unanimous King of football changed his sport forever.
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>
         <section class="article_page article_page--secondary js-article-page-26 cf display-none " data-page="26">
          <header class="article_page-header">

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             26. The Tale of Cal Ripken Jr.
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:265px">
            <img alt="26. The Tale of Cal Ripken Jr. " data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/584/188/Ripken-lap-1995_display_image_crop_north.jpg?w=265&amp;h=400&amp;q=75" height="400" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="265"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="265">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="265">
             <span itemprop="caption">
              Image via baltimoresportstalk.wordpress.com
             </span>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            September 6, 1995, was the day an ironman was cemented and a legacy glued. Eclipsing Lou Gehrig's consecutive games played was a record once deemed unbreakable.
           </p>
           <p>
            But the dynamic 19-time All-Star Oriole was a believer. He got the job done for 21 memorable years.
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>
         <section class="article_page article_page--secondary js-article-page-27 cf display-none " data-page="27">
          <header class="article_page-header">
           <div class="article_nav-bar br-texture--sudo br-texture--sudo-fade-to-white">
            <div class="paginators paginators--top">
             <a class="paginator paginator--secondary paginator--prev" href="javascript: void(0)" title="Previous Page">

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             25. David Tyree Uses His Head
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="25. David Tyree Uses His Head" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/583/484/hi-res-79498412_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="630">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">
             <span>
              Andy Lyons/Getty Images
             </span>
             <br/>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            There were few fans who didn't expect the roaring Patriots to complete their undefeated season in 2008.
           </p>
           <p>
            But thanks to the unlikely prowess of renowned special teamer-receiver David Tyree (and his helmet, of course) during the most epic Super Bowl in recent memory, the Giants did the impossible. The 18-1 Pats could only watch in awe as their feisty opponents stole the show.
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             24. Willis Reed's Limp
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:244px">
            <img alt="24. Willis Reed's Limp" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/583/004/willisreed300w_crop_north.jpg?w=244&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="244"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="244">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="244">
             <span itemprop="caption">
              Image via ihtraptors.blogspot.com
             </span>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            Because of a severe thigh injury that kept him out of Game 6, Knicks star Willis Reed was expected to miss Game 7 of the 1970 NBA Finals against the Lakers in Madison Square Garden.
           </p>
           <p>
            However, in perfect script-like fashion, Reed tiptoed onto the court during warmups to shocked roars and an appreciative, citywide applause. He would score the Knicks'  first two field goals on his first two shot attempts, setting an early tone for what would become New York City's first NBA title.
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>
         <section class="article_page article_page--secondary js-article-page-29 cf display-none " data-page="29">
          <header class="article_page-header">
           <div class="article_nav-bar br-texture--sudo br-texture--sudo-fade-to-white">
            <div class="paginators paginators--top">
             <a class="paginator paginator--secondary paginator--prev" href="javascript: void(0)" title="Previous Page">

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             23. Don Shula's Success
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="23. Don Shula's Success" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/583/987/nh27857822_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="630">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">
             <span itemprop="caption">
              Image via news-herald.com
             </span>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            Remembered as the ringleader of the only perfect season in NFL history, legendary coach Don Shula finally embraced the state of euphoria in 1993.
           </p>
           <p>
            Following his 325th victory on Nov. 14 of that year, Shula was carried off the field by his loyal Dolphins. He would retire two years later with a record 347 wins.
           </p>
           <p>
            "I think what coaching is all about, is taking players and analyzing there ability, put them in a position where they can excel within the framework of the team winning. And I hope that Ive done that in my 33 years as a head coach,"
            <a href="http://coacheshotseat.com/coacheshotseatblog/archives/4188" target="_blank">
             he said
            </a>
            .
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>
         <section class="article_page article_page--secondary js-article-page-30 cf display-none " data-page="30">
          <header class="article_page-header">
           <div class="article_nav-bar br-texture--sudo br-texture--sudo-fade-to-white">
            <div class="paginators paginators--top">
             <a class="paginator paginator--secondary paginator--prev" href="javascript: void(0)" title="Previous Page">

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             22. Kirk Gibson's Grit
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:280px">
            <img alt="22. Kirk Gibson's Grit" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/583/648/mlb_a_gibson01_400_crop_north.jpg?w=280&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="280"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="280">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="280">
             <span itemprop="caption">
              Image via sports.espn.go.com
             </span>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            Game 1 of the '88 World Series, Dodgers trailing the Athletics 4-3, ninth inning, two outsa moment when heroes are made.
           </p>
           <p>
            Because of a bad left hamstring and swollen right knee, Los Angeles star Kirk Gibson was stuck watching the series from the pine. But he did get one pinch-hit opportunity. And it was during this clutch moment that the slugger gripped the bat, clenched his teeth and swung for the fences against the game's best reliever, Dennis Eckersley. His home run and ensuing fist-pumping prance around the bases made believers out of skeptics.
           </p>
           <p>
            Dodgers win Game 1 by a score of 5-4 and the series in five.
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>
         <section class="article_page article_page--secondary js-article-page-31 cf display-none " data-page="31">

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             21. Chuck Bednarik's Knockout
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="21. Chuck Bednarik's Knockout" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/583/470/chuck-bednarik_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="630">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">
             <span itemprop="caption">
              Image via 4starcustoms.blogspot.com
             </span>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            When Philly's linebacker Chuck Bednarik, known around his parts as Concrete Charlie, demolished Giants star tailback Frank Gifford, the visual deflation would detail the animosity stuffed deep within a heated rivalry. Gifford's "
            <a href="http://www.nytimes.com/2010/11/21/sports/football/21anderson.html" target="_blank">
             deep brain concussion
            </a>
            " would keep him out 18 months and add a new chapter to the New York-Philadelphia saga.
           </p>
           <p>
            Eagles vs. Giants; as dicey as dicey gets.
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>
         <section class="article_page article_page--secondary js-article-page-32 cf display-none " data-page="32">

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             20. Derek Redmond's Courage
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:253px">
            <img alt="20. Derek Redmond's Courage" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/583/496/derek-redmond1_crop_north.jpg?w=253&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="253"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="253">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="253">
             <span itemprop="caption">
              Image via terrifictop10.wordpress.com
             </span>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            As Morgan Freeman brilliantly
            <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=VO8b-zIKixM" target="_blank">
             detailed
            </a>
            :
           </p>
           <blockquote>
            <p>
             Derek Redmond didnt finish in first place in the 1992 400-meter. He  didnt finish in second. Or third. Or fourth. He, and his father,  finished dead last. But he, and his father, finished.
            </p>
           </blockquote>
           <p>
            At the 1992 Olympic Games in Barcelona, the British track star did the impossible. Despite tearing his hamstring midway through the 400-meter semifinal, Redmond got up and battled for a lap. His father's assistance would become a heroic visual for years to come.
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>
         <section class="article_page article_page--secondary js-article-page-33 cf display-none " data-page="33">
          <header class="article_page-header">
           <div class="article_nav-bar br-texture--sudo br-texture--sudo-fade-to-white">

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             19. Muhammad Ali Lights the Torch
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:301px">
            <img alt="19. Muhammad Ali Lights the Torch" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/583/008/MuhammadAliholdsupthetorchpriortolightingadevicethatwouldcarrytheflameupthecauldron_crop_north.jpg?w=301&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="301"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="301">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="301">
             <span itemprop="caption">
              Image via mirror.co.uk
             </span>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            Arguably the greatest heavyweight of all time and easily the most recognizable figure in sports, Muhammad Ali made memories when he ignited the Olympic fire in 1996.
           </p>
           <p>
            Fighting the devastating effects of Parkinson's disease, Ali shook as he carried the torch. But his presence signified a historical moment. The man who once crossed every social boundary was now meshing them all.
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>
         <section class="article_page article_page--secondary js-article-page-34 cf display-none " data-page="34">
          <header class="article_page-header">
           <div class="article_nav-bar br-texture--sudo br-texture--sudo-fade-to-white">
            <div class="paginators paginators--top">

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             18. Wilt Chamberlain Scores 100
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:332px">
            <img alt="18. Wilt Chamberlain Scores 100" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/584/149/55196_web_Jocks-wilt-3-col-BW_crop_north.jpg?w=332&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="332"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="332">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="332">
             <span itemprop="caption">
              Image via thedailyworld.com
             </span>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            It was just over 50 years ago when Wilt the Stilt scored a monstrous 100 points against the Knicks as his Warriors rolled to a 169-147 victory.
           </p>
           <p>
            Often referred to as The Big Dipper, Chamberlain was a mountain of a man who could pour the rock into the basket with grace or slam it in with vigor. His 100-point record remains, with Kobe Bryant being the only one to come "close" with 81 points in a 2006 game.
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             17. Mudman
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="17. Mudman" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/583/472/COTTON_FRAN_LIONS_1977Csp-21-1_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="630">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">
             <span itemprop="caption">
              Image via colorsport.co.uk
             </span>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            English rugby icon Fran Cotton was immortalized by this 1977 mud shot, which featured British Lions forwards waiting for the match against the Junior All Blacks to end.
           </p>
           <p>
            A drenched war presents perhaps the most beloved shot in rugby history, captured perfectly by Colin Elsey.
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>
         <section class="article_page article_page--secondary js-article-page-36 cf display-none " data-page="36">
          <header class="article_page-header">
           <div class="article_nav-bar br-texture--sudo br-texture--sudo-fade-to-white">

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             16. Lou Gehrig's Farewell Speech
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:550px">
            <img alt="16. Lou Gehrig's Farewell Speech" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/583/620/1939_lou_gehrig_crop_north.jpg?w=550&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="550"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="550">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="550">
             <span itemprop="caption">
              Image via sportsthenandnow.com
             </span>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            Revered for his durability and humble nature, Yankees great Lou Gehrig knew it was time to call it quits when he was diagnosed with amyotrophic lateral sclerosis in June of 1939.
           </p>
           <p>
            His farewell speech inspired anyone with a pulse. "Today I consider myself the luckiest man on the face of the earth,"
            <a href="http://www.lougehrig.com/about/speech.htm" target="_blank">
             he said
            </a>
            . "I might have been given a bad break, but I've got an awful lot to live for."
           </p>
           <p>
            He would pass away two years later.
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>
         <section class="article_page article_page--secondary js-article-page-37 cf display-none " data-page="37">
          <header class="article_page-header">
           <div class="article_nav-bar br-texture--sudo br-texture--sudo-fade-to-white">
            <div class="paginators paginators--top">
             <a class="paginator paginator--secondary paginator--prev" href="javascript: void(0)" title="Previous Page">
              <span class="aquo">
               
              </span>

             </a>
             <div class="paginators_counter">

              <span class="br-light-grey">
               of
              </span>
              <span class="paginators_page-count">
               52
              </span>
             </div>
             <a class="paginator paginator--secondary paginator--next" href="javascript: void(0)" title="Next Page">

              <span class="aquo">
               
              </span>
             </a>

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             15. Paul Henderson's Summit Stunner
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:400px">
            <img alt="15. Paul Henderson's Summit Stunner" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/583/734/henderson1-1_crop_north.jpg?w=400&amp;h=354&amp;q=75" height="354" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="400"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="400">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="400">
             <span itemprop="caption">
              Image via carp.ca
             </span>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            Paul Henderson played 13 seasons in the NHL, but it was three games during the '72 Summit Series that made him a legend.
           </p>
           <p>
            A pivotal member of the Canadian team that upset the Soviets, Henderson scored the game-winning goals in the sixth, seventh and eighth games of  the 1972 series, the final one securing his immortality.
           </p>
           <p>
            He remains a Canadian hero, eh.
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>

              </span>
             </div>
             <a class="paginator paginator--secondary paginator--next" href="javascript: void(0)" title="Next Page">
              Next
              <span class="aquo">
               
              </span>
             </a>
            </div>
            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             14. Hank Aaron Becomes an Icon
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:520px">
            <img alt="14. Hank Aaron Becomes an Icon" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/583/884/6262679_f520_crop_north.jpg?w=520&amp;h=390&amp;q=75" height="390" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="520"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="520">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="520">
             <span itemprop="caption">
              Image via bdegiulio.hubpages.com
             </span>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            Hank Aaron's worldly destruction of Babe Ruth's home run record on April 8, 1974, off No. 44 Al Downing broke all of baseball's barriers, at least for that one moment. The diamond descent with two college students detailed the intensity of that home run. While racism flooded his career, Aaron was still a beloved icon.
           </p>
           <p>
            It was lyrically crafty broadcaster Vin Scully who
            <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=GvfYg_kNtTk&amp;feature=search" target="_blank">
             said it best
            </a>
            :
           </p>
           <blockquote>
            <p>
             What a marvelous moment for baseball; what a marvelous moment for  Atlanta and the state of Georgia; what a marvelous moment for the  country and the world. A black man is getting a standing ovation in the  Deep South for breaking a record of an all-time baseball idol. And it is  a great moment for all of us, and particularly for Henry Aaron And  for the first time in a long time, that poker face in Aaron shows the  tremendous strain and relief of what it must have been like to live with  for the past several months.
            </p>
           </blockquote>
          </div>
         </section>
         <section class="article_page article_page--secondary js-article-page-39 cf display-none " data-page="39">
          <header class="article_page-header">
           <div class="article_nav-bar br-texture--sudo br-texture--sudo-fade-to-white">

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             13. Michael Jordan's Last Hurrah
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:585px">
            <img alt="13. Michael Jordan's Last Hurrah" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/583/938/michael-jordan-bryon-russell_crop_north.jpg?w=585&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="585"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="585">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="585">
             <span itemprop="caption">
              Image via saltcityhoops.com
             </span>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            Michael Jordan's most historic shot was his last with the Bulls.
           </p>
           <p>
            Game 6 of the '98 Finals was the site, John Stockton's Jazz the opponents. But it was Jordan's ankle-breaking crossover and eventual drain over Bryon Russell that secured an 8786 victory, clinching Chicago's sixth
            <span class="mw-redirect">
             NBA title
            </span>
            in eight years.
           </p>
           <p>
            Russell seems
            <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=mrPf9Bch1pc" target="_blank">
             eager for payback
            </a>
            .
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>
