            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             12. Buster Douglas Upsets Iron Mike
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:536px">
            <img alt="12. Buster Douglas Upsets Iron Mike" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/583/438/tysondouglas_crop_north.jpg?w=536&amp;h=400&amp;q=75" height="400" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="536"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="536">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="536">
             <span itemprop="caption">
              Image via worldboxingnews.net
             </span>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            Those who had working pulses on February 11, 1990, could hardly believe what they'd saw. The undefeated heavyweightthe most feared man on Earthwas just beaten. Rather, demolished.
           </p>
           <p>
            Mike Tyson earned more than a busted lip from Buster Douglas in what became the biggest upset in boxing history. The 42-to-1 underdog sent the boxing world into shock.
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>
         <section class="article_page article_page--secondary js-article-page-41 cf display-none " data-page="41">

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             11. Bob Beamon's Perfect Jump
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:317px">
            <img alt="11. Bob Beamon's Perfect Jump" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/583/005/1007422_orig_crop_north.jpg?w=317&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="317"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="317">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="317">
             <span itemprop="caption">
              Image via vervesplash.net
             </span>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            Forget that Bob Beamon's long jump world record at the 1968 Mexico Olympics remained intact for almost 23 years, forget that it might have been the perfect jump. This was a leap so awe-inspiring that the measuring device became useless. The tape was
            <a href="http://sportsillustrated.cnn.com/vault/article/magazine/MAG1081936/index.htm" target="_blank">
             called on for assistance
            </a>
            .
           </p>
           <p>
            Beamon made us rethink what was humanly possible.
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             10. Jackie Robinson Pioneers the Way
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:335px">
            <img alt="10. Jackie Robinson Pioneers the Way" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/583/760/robinson_j_montreal_crop_north.jpg?w=335&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="335"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="335">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="335">
             <span itemprop="caption">
              Image via padresteve.com
             </span>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            When he debuted with the
            <span class="mw-redirect">
             Brooklyn Dodgers
            </span>
            in 1947 as the first African American to play in the major leagues in the live-ball era, Jackie Robinson changed sports forever.
           </p>
           <p>
            A jovial smile and firm grip on his bat was all it took for Robinson to help crush racial discrimination. This was his iconic ascent.
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             9. Y.A. Tittle's Bloody Defeat
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="9. Y.A. Tittle's Bloody Defeat" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/584/138/y.a.-tittle_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="630">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">
             <span itemprop="caption">
              Image via sikids.com
             </span>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            He was never the most talented, but Y.A. Tittle was always the gutsiest.
           </p>
           <p>
            Apparently suffering from
            <a href="http://www.manlyweb.com/sports/injuries/yatittle.htm" target="_blank">
             broken ribs
            </a>
            and a crushed ego during his final season of his Giants career, Tittle is photographed by
            <a href="http://www.smithsonianmag.com/people-places/fallen_giant.html" target="_blank">
             Morris Berman
            </a>
            kneeling down in defeat, bloodied and bruised. Passionate, determined, heroic.
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             8. The Hand of God
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:312px">
            <img alt="8. The Hand of God" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/583/536/diego-maradona-hand-of-god1_crop_north.jpg?w=312&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="312"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="312">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="312">
             <span itemprop="caption">
              Image via soccerjones.com
             </span>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            En route to its 1986 World Cup victory, the Argentina national football team found itself at the center of some intense controversy.
           </p>
           <p>
            During his team's 2-1 quarterfinal victory over England, legend Diego Maradona scored two goals. His first, later dubbed the "Hand of God," remains to this day the most scrutinized score in World Cup history.
           </p>
           <p>
            In the words of Maradona,
            <a href="http://www.thesun.co.uk/sol/homepage/news/745800/Diego-Maradona-Football-legend-finally-says-sorry-for-that-goal.html" target="_blank">
             the goal was scored
            </a>
            "a little with the head of Maradona and a little with the hand of God."
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>
         <section class="article_page article_page--secondary js-article-page-45 cf display-none " data-page="45">

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             7. Bobby Orr Soars to Greatness
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:529px">
            <img alt="7. Bobby Orr Soars to Greatness" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/584/071/orr_crop_north.jpg?w=529&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="529"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="529">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="529">
             <span itemprop="caption">
              Image via bobbyorrhalloffame.com
             </span>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            Before their was Niklas Lidstrom, there was Bobby Orr.
           </p>
           <p>
            Orr revolutionized the defenseman position, becoming a legitimate scoring threat while also shutting down forwards. His 46 goals in the 1974-75 season were simply unheard of.
           </p>
           <p>
            Thanks to photographer Ray Lussier, Orr's 1970 Stanley Cup-winning goal 40 seconds into overtime for the Bruins was captured brilliantly.
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             6. The Catch
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="6. The Catch" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/583/469/TheCatchDwightClark1980_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="630">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">
             <span itemprop="caption">
              Image via thecitrusreport.com
             </span>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            Dwight Clark's bulbous fingers clinging to pigskin life signaled the end of Dallas' NFC domination and the start of San Francisco's '80s dynasty.
           </p>
           <p>
            This breathtaking shot was the winning touchdown toss by cool Joe Montana in the epic 1982 NFC Championship Game. On third-and-three with 58 seconds left, Montana to Clark left football fans in awe.
            <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1981%E2%80%9382_NFL_playoffs#NFC:_San_Francisco_49ers_28.2C_Dallas_Cowboys_27" title="198182 NFL playoffs">
             <br/>
            </a>
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>
         <section class="article_page article_page--secondary js-article-page-47 cf display-none " data-page="47">
          <header class="article_page-header">
           <div class="article_nav-bar br-texture--sudo br-texture--sudo-fade-to-white">
            <div class="paginators paginators--top">
             <a class="paginator paginator--secondary paginator--prev" href="javascript: void(0)" title="Previous Page">

              <span class="br-light-grey">

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             5. Roger Bannister Breaks the Mark
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="5. Roger Bannister Breaks the Mark" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/584/202/roger-bannister_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="630">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">
             <span itemprop="caption">
              Image via sportsillustrated.cnn.com
             </span>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            Long before becoming a distinguished neurologist, Roger Bannister broke a record few believed humanly possible. A mark no runner had ever crossed.
           </p>
           <p>
            The 1954 Sportsman of the Year ran the first sub-four-minute mile, crossing the line to the roars of astonished viewers. On May 6, 1954, during a meet between
            <span class="mw-redirect">
             British AAA
            </span>
            and
            <span class="mw-redirect">
             Oxford University, Bannister earned a time of
             <a href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/onthisday/hi/witness/may/6/newsid_3686000/3686793.stm" target="_blank">
              three minutes and 59.4 seconds
             </a>
             .
            </span>
           </p>
           <p>
            The impossible was now possible.
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>
         <section class="article_page article_page--secondary js-article-page-48 cf display-none " data-page="48">
          <header class="article_page-header">
           <div class="article_nav-bar br-texture--sudo br-texture--sudo-fade-to-white">
            <div class="paginators paginators--top">
             <a class="paginator paginator--secondary paginator--prev" href="javascript: void(0)" title="Previous Page">
              <span class="aquo">
               
              </span>
              Prev
             </a>
             <div class="paginators_counter">
              48
              <span class="br-light-grey">
               of
              </span>
              <span class="paginators_page-count">
               52
              </span>
             </div>
             <a class="paginator paginator--secondary paginator--next" href="javascript: void(0)" title="Next Page">

              <span class="aquo">
               
              </span>
             </a>
            </div>
            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             4. The Miracle on Ice
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:546px">
            <img alt="4. The Miracle on Ice" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/583/953/gal-upsets-miracle-jpg_crop_north.jpg?w=546&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="546"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="546">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="546">
             <span itemprop="caption">
              Image via nydailynews.com
             </span>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            On an icy Lake Placid night in 1980, the Herb Brooks-led Americans brought home arguably the most riveting victory in the history of sports.
           </p>
           <p>
            With the Soviets having won the previous four ice hockey gold medals dating back to the 1964 games, few gave the amateur and collegiate Americans a chance. Cold War emotions only added intrigue to an already brutal rivalry.
           </p>
           <p>
            But in 1980, the U.S. squad completed the impossible, defeating the Soviets before moving on to the final and making another comeback, this time over Finland for the gold medal. Since then, we've fully believed in miracles.
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>
         <section class="article_page article_page--secondary js-article-page-49 cf display-none " data-page="49">
          <header class="article_page-header">
           <div class="article_nav-bar br-texture--sudo br-texture--sudo-fade-to-white">
            <div class="paginators paginators--top">
             <a class="paginator paginator--secondary paginator--prev" href="javascript: void(0)" title="Previous Page">
              <span class="aquo">
               
              </span>
              Prev
             </a>
             <div class="paginators_counter">
              49
              <span class="br-light-grey">
               of
              </span>
              <span class="paginators_page-count">
               52
              </span>
             </div>
             <a class="paginator paginator--secondary paginator--next" href="javascript: void(0)" title="Next Page">
              Next
              <span class="aquo">
               
              </span>
             </a>
            </div>
            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             3. Jesse Owens' Victory
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:293px">
            <img alt="3. Jesse Owens' Victory" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/583/773/jesse-owens_display_image_crop_north.jpg?w=293&amp;h=400&amp;q=75" height="400" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="293"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="293">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="293">
             <span itemprop="caption">
              Image via iconicphotos.wordpress.com
             </span>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            Known statistically as the most successful athlete at the 1936 Berlin Games, track star Jesse Owens eclipsed what many believed was Adolf Hitler's Aryan showcase by securing four gold medals and the hearts of fans worldwide (
            <a href="http://espn.go.com/sportscentury/features/00016393.html" target="_blank">
             and three world records in 45 minutes
            </a>
            ).
           </p>
           <p>
            Owens proved that he was no routine, society-abiding athlete. He was a hero.
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>
         <section class="article_page article_page--secondary js-article-page-50 cf display-none " data-page="50">
          <header class="article_page-header">
           <div class="article_nav-bar br-texture--sudo br-texture--sudo-fade-to-white">
            <div class="paginators paginators--top">
             <a class="paginator paginator--secondary paginator--prev" href="javascript: void(0)" title="Previous Page">
              <span class="aquo">
               
              </span>
              Prev
             </a>
             <div class="paginators_counter">
              50
              <span class="br-light-grey">
               of
              </span>
              <span class="paginators_page-count">
               52
              </span>
             </div>
             <a class="paginator paginator--secondary paginator--next" href="javascript: void(0)" title="Next Page">
              Next
              <span class="aquo">
               
              </span>
             </a>
            </div>
            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             2. The Human Rights Salute
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:351px">
            <img alt="2. The Human Rights Salute" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/583/445/article-1341928393926-13EF3870000005DC-901640_466x557_crop_north.jpg?w=351&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="351"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="351">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="351">
             <span itemprop="caption">
              Image via metro.co.uk
             </span>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            Tommie Smith and John Carlos each won medals in the 200-meter dash back in 1968 (Smith's 19.83seconds marking the first time the 20-second barrier was broken). During the victory ceremony, they admirably bowed their heads and thrust their black-gloved fists toward the sky.
           </p>
           <p>
            Their inspirational performance on the podium stand became one of the most iconic images of the Black Panther Movement, which intended to end racial inequality in politics and on the streets. "Black America will understand what we did tonight,"
            <a href="http://colorlines.com/archives/2011/10/on_this_day_two_african-american_olympians_make_silent_protest_heard_around_the_world.html" target="_blank">
             said Smith
            </a>
            .
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>
         <section class="article_page article_page--secondary js-article-page-51 cf display-none " data-page="51">
          <header class="article_page-header">
           <div class="article_nav-bar br-texture--sudo br-texture--sudo-fade-to-white">
            <div class="paginators paginators--top">
             <a class="paginator paginator--secondary paginator--prev" href="javascript: void(0)" title="Previous Page">
              <span class="aquo">
               
              </span>
              Prev
             </a>
             <div class="paginators_counter">
              51
              <span class="br-light-grey">
               of
              </span>
              <span class="paginators_page-count">
               52
              </span>
             </div>
             <a class="paginator paginator--secondary paginator--next" href="javascript: void(0)" title="Next Page">
              Next
              <span class="aquo">
               
              </span>
             </a>
            </div>
            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             1. Muhammad Ali's Phantom Punch
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="1. Muhammad Ali's Phantom Punch" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/583/009/muhammad-ali-sonny-liston-001068644_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="630">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">
             <span itemprop="caption">
              Image via sportsillustrated.cnn.com
             </span>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            When 22-year-old phenom Muhammad Ali (then Cassius Clay) defeated 32-year-old Sonny Liston to become the world heavyweight champion, fans were stunned and immediately enamored. Their rematch would be captured in this one controversial moment. One minute and 40 seconds into the fight, Liston went down following Ali's supposed "phantom punch."
           </p>
           <p>
            In the end,
            <a href="http://mirroreyes.wordpress.com/2010/02/14/phantompunch/" target="_blank">
             Neil Leifer's shot
            </a>
            engulfed everything Ali represented. Strength, speed and bravado.
           </p>
           <p>
            Ali became the truest of legends.
           </p>
           <p>
           </p>
           <p>
            <em>
             Follow me for more Iconography.
            </em>
           </p>
           <p>
            <a class="twitter-follow-button" href="https://twitter.com/z_pumerantz">
             Follow @z_pumerantz
            </a>
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>
